ps[i].Scope)\n\t}\n\n\t// Reduce wildcards\n\tfor action, wildcards := range wildcardsByAction {\n\t\tfor wildcard := range wildcards {\n\t\t\tif wildcard == \"*\" {\n\t\t\t\treduced[action] = []string{wildcard}\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif includes(wildcards, wildcard[:len(wildcard)-2]) {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treduced[action] = append(reduced[action], wildcard)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Reduce specific\n\tfor action, scopes := range scopesByAction {\n\t\tfor scope := range scopes {\n\t\t\tif includes(wildcardsByAction[action], scope) {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treduced[action] = append(reduced[action], scope)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn reduced\n}\n\nfunc ValidateScope(scope string) bool {\n\tprefix, last := scope[:len(scope)-1], scope[len(scope)-1]\n\t// verify that last char is either ':' or '/' if last character of scope is '*'\n\tif len(prefix) > 0 && last == '*' {\n\t\tlastChar := prefix[len(prefix)-1]\n\t\tif lastChar != ':' && lastChar != '/' {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn !strings.ContainsAny(prefix, \"*?\")\n}\n\nfunc ManagedUserRoleName(userID int64) string {\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"managed:users:%d:permissions\", userID)\n}\n\nfunc ManagedTeamRoleName(teamID int64) string {\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"managed:teams:%d:permissions\", teamID)\n}\n\nfunc ManagedBuiltInRoleName(builtInRole string) string {\n\treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"managed:builtins:%s:permissions\", strings.ToLower(builtInRole))\n}\n\n// GetOrgRoles returns legacy org roles for a three-tier permission model (Viewer/Editor/Admin) is defined and enforced across the following layers:\\n\\n## 1. Role Type Definition (`pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go`)\\n\\nThe canonical definition of `RoleType` lives in the identity package. It declares `RoleViewer`, `RoleEditor`, and `RoleAdmin` as string constants, along with a `rolePrecedence` map (None=10, Viewer=20, Editor=30, Admin=40) that powers the `Includes()` method — making Admin include Editor which includes Viewer. The `Children()` and `Parents()` helpers derive role hierarchy from precedence. These are re-exported in `pkg/services/org/model.go` as `org.RoleViewer`, `org.RoleEditor`, `org.RoleAdmin`.\\n\\n## 2. Role-to-Permission Mapping\\n\\n### Basic Role Definitions (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go`)\\n`BuildBasicRoleDefinitions()` creates the in-memory `RoleDTO` objects for each of the five basic roles (None, Viewer, Editor, Admin, Grafana Admin). `DeclareFixedRoles()` wires built-in fixed roles (LDAP, org users, settings, stats, users) to Grafana Admin. The `RoleRegistration.Grants` field throughout the codebase specifies which org-role tiers receive each fixed role.\\n\\n### API-level Fixed Role Grants (`pkg/api/accesscontrol.go`)\\n`HTTPServer.declareFixedRoles()` declares all the major fixed roles the HTTP API needs and assigns them to Viewer/Editor/Admin tiers. Examples: `datasourcesExplorerRole` → Editor, `datasourcesReaderRole` → Admin (or Viewer when license enforcement is off), `annotationsReaderRole` → Viewer, `annotationsWriterRole` → Editor, `dashboardsCreatorRole` → Editor, `dashboardsWriterRole` → Admin, `orgReaderRole` → Viewer, `orgWriterRole` → Admin.\\n\\n### Dashboard Permission Actions (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go`)\\nDefines the three-tier action sets for dashboards:\\n- `DashboardViewActions`: `[dashboards:read]`\\n- `DashboardEditActions`: View + `[dashboards:write, dashboards:delete]`\\n- `DashboardAdminActions`: Edit + `[dashboards.permissions:read, dashboards.permissions:write]`\\n`registerDashboardRoles()` seeds `fixed:dashboards:viewer/editor/admin` and grants them to Viewer/Editor/Admin respectively. `ProvideDashboardPermissions()` creates the resource permissions service with `PermissionsToActions` mapping View/Edit/Admin strings to action lists.\\n\\n### Folder Permission Actions (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go`)\\nSimilarly defines `FolderViewActions`, `FolderEditActions`, `FolderAdminActions` (which include alerting rule and library panel actions). `registerFolderRoles()` and `ProvideFolderPermissions()` set up the equivalent three-tier action mapping for folder resources.\\n\\n### Dashboard/Folder Access Constants (`pkg/services/dashboards/dashboardaccess/dashboard_access.go`)\\nDefines the legacy `PermissionType` iota: `PERMISSION_VIEW=1`, `PERMISSION_EDIT=2`, `PERMISSION_ADMIN=4`, used in legacy ACL-based permission checks.\\n\\n## 3. Permission Guard Middleware\\n\\n### Legacy Role Guards (`pkg/middleware/auth.go` and `pkg/middleware/middleware.go`)\\n`RoleAuth(roles ...org.RoleType)` in `auth.go` is the fundamental role-based gate: it checks `c.OrgRole == role` for any of the supplied roles and calls `accessForbidden()` if none match. `Auth(options)` handles signed-in and Grafana admin checks. In `middleware.go`, pre-built guards are exposed as package-level vars:\\n- `ReqEditorRole = RoleAuth(org.RoleEditor, org.RoleAdmin)` — allows Editor or Admin\\n- `ReqOrgAdmin = RoleAuth(org.RoleAdmin)` — allows only Admin\\n- `ReqGrafanaAdmin` — requires server admin flag\\n\\n### RBAC Middleware (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go`)\\n`Middleware(ac AccessControl)` returns a `web.Handler` factory for fine-grained RBAC guards. It calls `authorize(c, ac, user, evaluator)` which invokes `ac.Evaluate()` with scope-injected evaluators. On failure, `deny()` returns HTTP 403. `AuthorizeInOrgMiddleware()` handles cross-org authorization. `ReqHasRole()` in `accesscontrol.go` wraps `c.HasRole()` as an evaluator predicate.\\n\\n### AccessControl Interface and Evaluators (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/accesscontrol.go`, `evaluator.go`)\\n`AccessControl.Evaluate()` is the central permission check. `EvalPermission(action, scopes...)` creates a `permissionEvaluator` that matches the user's permission map. `EvalAll`/`EvalAny` compose evaluators.\\n\\n### Core Implementation (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/`)\\n`acimpl.AccessControl.Evaluate()` merges in-memory basic role permissions with DB-stored managed permissions. `Service.getUserPermissions()` calls `GetOrgRoles(user)` (which returns the user's role and parent roles via the precedence hierarchy) to look up basic role permissions, then fetches managed role permissions from the DB via the store.\\n\\n### User Role Resolution (`pkg/services/user/identity.go`)\\n`SignedInUser.HasRole(role)` returns true if the user is a Grafana admin OR if `u.OrgRole.Includes(role)` — i.e., the role hierarchy check. `GetOrgRole()` returns the assigned tier.\\n\\n## 4. Folder/Dashboard Permission Inheritance\\n\\n### Scope Resolvers (`pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go`)\\nPermission inheritance is implemented through scope resolution. `GetInheritedScopes()` traverses the folder tree upward via `folderSvc.GetParents()` and returns a slice of `folders:uid:<uid>` scopes for all ancestor folders. This means a permission granted on a parent folder applies to all nested folders and dashboards.\\n\\n`NewFolderUIDScopeResolver()` and `NewFolderIDScopeResolver()` convert legacy folder-id scopes into UID-based scopes, appending inherited parent scopes.\\n\\n`NewDashboardUIDScopeResolver()` and `NewDashboardIDScopeResolver()` call `resolveDashboardScope()`, which looks up the dashboard's `FolderUID` and returns the dashboard scope plus the folder scope chain (via `GetInheritedScopes()`). This is how dashboard permissions inherit from their containing folders.\\n\\n### Folder Service (`pkg/services/folder/folderimpl/folder.go`, `pkg/services/folder/model.go`)\\nThe `Folder` struct stores `ParentUID` and `FullpathUIDs` for efficient ancestor traversal. The `Service` provides `GetParents()` used by `GetInheritedScopes()`.\\n\\n### Resource Permissions Store (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/resourcepermissions/store.go`)\\n`flatResourcePermission.IsInherited(scope)` returns true for managed permissions whose scope does not directly match the requested resource (i.e., they come from a parent folder). This powers the display of inherited vs. direct permissions in the UI.\\n\\n### Folder/Dashboard Resource Permission Services (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/`)\\n`ProvideFolderPermissions()` and `ProvideDashboardPermissions()` both configure an `InheritedScopesSolver` callback that calls `GetInheritedScopes()`, wiring the inheritance mechanism into the resource permissions evaluation engine.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1782,"cache_read_input_tokens":96983,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1782,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"c130fcfb-38c5-4aa9-b853-fbc1455ccabd","uuid":"9a8fc290-326a-4999-b710-1b4900d7d04a"}

three-tier permission model (Viewer/Editor/Admin) is defined and enforced across the following layers:\\n\\n## 1. Role Type Definition (`pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go`)\\n\\nThe canonical definition of `RoleType` lives in the identity package. It declares `RoleViewer`, `RoleEditor`, and `RoleAdmin` as string constants, along with a `rolePrecedence` map (None=10, Viewer=20, Editor=30, Admin=40) that powers the `Includes()` method — making Admin include Editor which includes Viewer. The `Children()` and `Parents()` helpers derive role hierarchy from precedence. These are re-exported in `pkg/services/org/model.go` as `org.RoleViewer`, `org.RoleEditor`, `org.RoleAdmin`.\\n\\n## 2. Role-to-Permission Mapping\\n\\n### Basic Role Definitions (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go`)\\n`BuildBasicRoleDefinitions()` creates the in-memory `RoleDTO` objects for each of the five basic roles (None, Viewer, Editor, Admin, Grafana Admin). `DeclareFixedRoles()` wires built-in fixed roles (LDAP, org users, settings, stats, users) to Grafana Admin. The `RoleRegistration.Grants` field throughout the codebase specifies which org-role tiers receive each fixed role.\\n\\n### API-level Fixed Role Grants (`pkg/api/accesscontrol.go`)\\n`HTTPServer.declareFixedRoles()` declares all the major fixed roles the HTTP API needs and assigns them to Viewer/Editor/Admin tiers. Examples: `datasourcesExplorerRole` → Editor, `datasourcesReaderRole` → Admin (or Viewer when license enforcement is off), `annotationsReaderRole` → Viewer, `annotationsWriterRole` → Editor, `dashboardsCreatorRole` → Editor, `dashboardsWriterRole` → Admin, `orgReaderRole` → Viewer, `orgWriterRole` → Admin.\\n\\n### Dashboard Permission Actions (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go`)\\nDefines the three-tier action sets for dashboards:\\n- `DashboardViewActions`: `[dashboards:read]`\\n- `DashboardEditActions`: View + `[dashboards:write, dashboards:delete]`\\n- `DashboardAdminActions`: Edit + `[dashboards.permissions:read, dashboards.permissions:write]`\\n`registerDashboardRoles()` seeds `fixed:dashboards:viewer/editor/admin` and grants them to Viewer/Editor/Admin respectively. `ProvideDashboardPermissions()` creates the resource permissions service with `PermissionsToActions` mapping View/Edit/Admin strings to action lists.\\n\\n### Folder Permission Actions (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go`)\\nSimilarly defines `FolderViewActions`, `FolderEditActions`, `FolderAdminActions` (which include alerting rule and library panel actions). `registerFolderRoles()` and `ProvideFolderPermissions()` set up the equivalent three-tier action mapping for folder resources.\\n\\n### Dashboard/Folder Access Constants (`pkg/services/dashboards/dashboardaccess/dashboard_access.go`)\\nDefines the legacy `PermissionType` iota: `PERMISSION_VIEW=1`, `PERMISSION_EDIT=2`, `PERMISSION_ADMIN=4`, used in legacy ACL-based permission checks.\\n\\n## 3. Permission Guard Middleware\\n\\n### Legacy Role Guards (`pkg/middleware/auth.go` and `pkg/middleware/middleware.go`)\\n`RoleAuth(roles ...org.RoleType)` in `auth.go` is the fundamental role-based gate: it checks `c.OrgRole == role` for any of the supplied roles and calls `accessForbidden()` if none match. `Auth(options)` handles signed-in and Grafana admin checks. In `middleware.go`, pre-built guards are exposed as package-level vars:\\n- `ReqEditorRole = RoleAuth(org.RoleEditor, org.RoleAdmin)` — allows Editor or Admin\\n- `ReqOrgAdmin = RoleAuth(org.RoleAdmin)` — allows only Admin\\n- `ReqGrafanaAdmin` — requires server admin flag\\n\\n### RBAC Middleware (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go`)\\n`Middleware(ac AccessControl)` returns a `web.Handler` factory for fine-grained RBAC guards. It calls `authorize(c, ac, user, evaluator)` which invokes `ac.Evaluate()` with scope-injected evaluators. On failure, `deny()` returns HTTP 403. `AuthorizeInOrgMiddleware()` handles cross-org authorization. `ReqHasRole()` in `accesscontrol.go` wraps `c.HasRole()` as an evaluator predicate.\\n\\n### AccessControl Interface and Evaluators (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/accesscontrol.go`, `evaluator.go`)\\n`AccessControl.Evaluate()` is the central permission check. `EvalPermission(action, scopes...)` creates a `permissionEvaluator` that matches the user's permission map. `EvalAll`/`EvalAny` compose evaluators.\\n\\n### Core Implementation (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/`)\\n`acimpl.AccessControl.Evaluate()` merges in-memory basic role permissions with DB-stored managed permissions. `Service.getUserPermissions()` calls `GetOrgRoles(user)` (which returns the user's role and parent roles via the precedence hierarchy) to look up basic role permissions, then fetches managed role permissions from the DB via the store.\\n\\n### User Role Resolution (`pkg/services/user/identity.go`)\\n`SignedInUser.HasRole(role)` returns true if the user is a Grafana admin OR if `u.OrgRole.Includes(role)` — i.e., the role hierarchy check. `GetOrgRole()` returns the assigned tier.\\n\\n## 4. Folder/Dashboard Permission Inheritance\\n\\n### Scope Resolvers (`pkg/services/dashboards/accesscontrol.go`)\\nPermission inheritance is implemented through scope resolution. `GetInheritedScopes()` traverses the folder tree upward via `folderSvc.GetParents()` and returns a slice of `folders:uid:<uid>` scopes for all ancestor folders. This means a permission granted on a parent folder applies to all nested folders and dashboards.\\n\\n`NewFolderUIDScopeResolver()` and `NewFolderIDScopeResolver()` convert legacy folder-id scopes into UID-based scopes, appending inherited parent scopes.\\n\\n`NewDashboardUIDScopeResolver()` and `NewDashboardIDScopeResolver()` call `resolveDashboardScope()`, which looks up the dashboard's `FolderUID` and returns the dashboard scope plus the folder scope chain (via `GetInheritedScopes()`). This is how dashboard permissions inherit from their containing folders.\\n\\n### Folder Service (`pkg/services/folder/folderimpl/folder.go`, `pkg/services/folder/model.go`)\\nThe `Folder` struct stores `ParentUID` and `FullpathUIDs` for efficient ancestor traversal. The `Service` provides `GetParents()` used by `GetInheritedScopes()`.\\n\\n### Resource Permissions Store (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/resourcepermissions/store.go`)\\n`flatResourcePermission.IsInherited(scope)` returns true for managed permissions whose scope does not directly match the requested resource (i.e., they come from a parent folder). This powers the display of inherited vs. direct permissions in the UI.\\n\\n### Folder/Dashboard Resource Permission Services (`pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/`)\\n`ProvideFolderPermissions()` and `ProvideDashboardPermissions()` both configure an `InheritedScopesSolver` callback that calls `GetInheritedScopes()`, wiring the inheritance mechanism into the resource permissions evaluation engine.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
